Administer Flebogamma 5% DIF only by IV infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Do not dilute;<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> do not mix with other drugs, IV infusion fluids, or other IGIV preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

If large doses are to be administered, contents of several vials may be pooled into an empty, sterile IV infusion container using aseptic technique.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Discard any partially used vials.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Primary immunodeficiency: Administer Flebogamma 5% DIF at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.01 mL/kg per minute (0.5 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> If tolerated for first 30 minutes, may gradually increase IV infusion rate to a maximum of 0.1 mL/kg per minute (5 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Patients ≥65 years of age or at increased risk for renal dysfunction or thrombosis: Use minimum infusion rate practicable.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> IV infusion rate in geriatric patients should be <0.06 mL/kg per minute (<3 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Administer Flebogamma 10% DIF only by IV infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Do not dilute;<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> do not mix with other drugs, IV infusion fluids, or other IGIV preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

If large doses are to be administered, contents of several vials may be pooled into an empty, sterile IV infusion container using aseptic technique.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Discard any partially used vials and administration sets.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Primary immunodeficiency: Administer Flebogamma 10% DIF at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.01 mL/kg per minute (1 mg/kg per minute) for 30 minutes;<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> if tolerated, may gradually increase IV infusion rate to 0.04 mL/kg per minute (4 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> If tolerated, may gradually increase to a maximum rate of 0.08 mL/kg per minute (8 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

ITP: Administer Flebogamma 10% DIF at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.01 mL/kg per minute (1 mg/kg per minute) for 30 minutes;<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> if tolerated, may gradually increase IV infusion rate to 0.04 mL/kg per minute (4 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> May gradually increase to a maximum rate of 0.08 mL/kg per minute (8 mg/kg per minute) if tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Patients ≥65 years of age or at risk for renal dysfunction or thrombosis: Use minimum infusion rate practicable.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> IV infusion rate in geriatric patients should be <0.04 mL/kg per minute (<4 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Administer Gammagard Liquid 10% by IV infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Alternatively, may be administered by sub-Q infusion for primary immunodeficiency (see Sub-Q Administration of Gammagard Liquid 10% under Dosage and Administration).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Do not mix with other drugs or other IGIV preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Do not shake.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Use of an in-line filter is optional.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> IV infusion line may be flushed with 0.9% sodium chloride injection.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Administer at room temperature;<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> do not warm in microwave.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Vials are for single use only.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Available as a 10% solution.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> If necessary, may be diluted with 5% dextrose injection;<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> do not use 0.9% sodium chloride as diluent.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> For solution compatibility information, see Compatibility under Stability.

Primary humoral immunodeficiency: Administer Gammagard Liquid 10% at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.5 mL/kg per hour (0.8 mg/kg per minute) for 30 minutes.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> IV infusion rate may be increased every 30 minutes (if tolerated) up to a maximum of 5 mL/kg per hour (8 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Maintenance treatment of MMN: Administer Gammagard Liquid 10% at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.5 mL/kg per hour (0.8 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> IV infusion rate may be increased (if tolerated) up to a maximum of 5.4 mL/kg per hour (9 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Patients >65 years of age or at risk for renal dysfunction or thrombosis: Use minimum IV infusion rate practicable.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> IV infusion rate in such patients should be <2 mL/kg per hour (<3.3 mg/kg per minute).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Administer Gammagard S/D only by IV infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Infuse via the administration set provided by the manufacturer, which contains an integral airway and a 15-µm filter;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> if this administration set not used, a similar filter must be used.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Use the antecubital vein for IV infusion whenever possible, especially when a 10% solution used;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> this may reduce infusion site discomfort.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Administer reconstituted Gammagard S/D through a separate IV line;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> do not mix with other drugs, IV infusion fluids, or other IGIV preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Administer at room temperature.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Reconstitute Gammagard S/D according to the manufacturer’s directions with the sterile water for injection diluent and transfer device provided to prepare a solution containing 50 or 100 mg of protein per mL (5 or 10% solution, respectively).<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Prior to reconstitution, allow powder for injection and diluent to warm to room temperature.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

After diluent added, gently rotate vial to dissolve the drug;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> to avoid foaming, do not shake.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

When large doses are to be administered, contents of several vials may be pooled into an empty, sterile IV infusion container using aseptic technique.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

If reconstituted outside of sterile laminar airflow conditions, administer within 2 hours after reconstitution (preferably as soon as possible).<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> If reconstituted in a sterile laminar flow hood using aseptic technique and reconstituted solution stored under constant refrigeration (2–8°C), administer within 24 hours after reconstitution (preferably as soon as possible).<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Discard any partially used vials.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Administer Gammagard S/D initially as a 5% solution at an initial IV infusion rate of 0.5 mL/kg per hour;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> if tolerated, may gradually increase IV infusion rate of 5% solution to a maximum of 4 mL/kg per hour.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> If further tolerated, may administer subsequent doses as a 10% solution given initially at an IV infusion rate of 0.5 mL/kg per hour;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> if tolerated, may gradually increase IV infusion rate of 10% solution to a maximum of 8 mL/kg per hour.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Patients at increased risk for renal dysfunction or thrombosis: Use minimum rate practicable.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Manufacturer recommends maximum IV infusion rate of <3.3 mg/kg per minute (<4 mL/kg per hour as a 5% solution or <2 mL/kg per hour as a 10% solution).<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> However, data not available to date to identify maximum safe concentration or IV infusion rate in patients at risk for renal dysfunction.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Patients who have not previously received Privigen 10% (or other immune globulin preparation), patients who have not received the drug within the past 8 weeks, and patients switching from another immune globulin preparation to Privigen 10%: May be at risk of developing inflammatory reactions if rapid IV infusion rate (e.g., >4 mg/kg per minute [>0.04 mL/kg per minute]) used.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Initiate Privigen10% in such patients using a slow IV infusion rate (e.g., ≤0.5 mg/kg per minute [≤0.005 mL/kg per minute]) and increase rate gradually to maximum rate tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Prior to initiation of sub-Q infusion, ensure that patients are not volume depleted and are adequately hydrated.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

In general, initiate using lowest recommended sub-Q infusion rate and slowly increase to maximum recommended rate as tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

If adverse reactions occur during sub-Q infusion, decrease rate of infusion or stop the infusion until reactions subside.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Use minimum dose and minimum sub-Q infusion rate practicable in patients at risk for thrombosis.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Administer Cutaquig 16.5% only by sub-Q infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

May be self-administered in the home or other appropriate setting;<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> provide patient and/or their caregiver with instructions and training regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Administer undiluted;<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> do not mix with other drugs, IV infusion fluids, or other immune globulin preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Vials are for single use only;<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> discard partially used vials.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Make sub-Q infusions into abdomen, thighs, upper arms, and/or upper leg/hips using an infusion pump;<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> avoid scars, tattoos, and any injured or inflamed areas.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Dose may be divided and infused simultaneously in up to 6 different infusion sites that are ≥2 inches apart.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> For those who have not previously received immune globulin subcutaneous, maximum volume of Cutaquig 16.5% per infusion site is 25 mL;<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> after first 5 doses, volume may be gradually increased to a maximum of 40 mL per infusion site as tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Rotate sub-Q infusion sites for each subsequent dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Consult manufacturer’s instructions provided with Cutaquig 16.5% and with the infusion pump for specific information regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Primary immunodeficiency: Administer first 6 sub-Q infusions of Cutaquig 16.5% at an infusion rate of 15–20 mL/hour at each infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> For subsequent sub-Q infusions, may increase infusion rate as tolerated to a maximum of 25 mL/hour at each infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Administer Cuvitru 20% only by sub-Q infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

May be self-administered sub-Q in the home or other appropriate setting;<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> provide patient and/or their caregiver with instructions and training regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Make sub-Q infusions into abdomen, thighs, upper arms, and/or lateral hip area;<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> avoid bony areas, visible blood vessels, scars, and any areas with inflammation (irritation) or infection.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Dose may be divided and infused simultaneously in up to 4 different infusion sites that are ≥4 inches apart;<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> use of a multi-needle administration set facilitates simultaneous sub-Q infusion at multiple sites.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Number of sites depends on volume of the dose;<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> calculate by dividing total volume to be infused by maximum volume per site.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> For first 2 sub-Q infusions, maximum volume per site is 20 mL in those weighing <40 kg or 60 mL in those weighing ≥40 kg;<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> maximum volume per site for subsequent infusions is 60 mL regardless of weight.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Consult manufacturer’s instructions provided with Cuvitru 20% and with the infusion pump for specific information regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Primary immunodeficiency: Administer first 2 sub-Q infusions of Cuvitru 20% at an infusion rate of 10–20 mL/hour at each infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> For subsequent sub-Q infusions, may increase infusion rate as tolerated to a maximum of 60 mL/hour at each infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Gammagard Liquid 10% may be administered by sub-Q infusion for treatment of primary immunodeficiency.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Also may be administered by IV infusion (see IV Administration of Gammagard Liquid 10% under Dosage and Administration).<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Primary immunodeficiency in patients weighing <40 kg: For initial sub-Q infusion of Gammagard Liquid 10%, use a volume of 20 mL per site and an infusion rate of 15 mL/hour per site.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> For maintenance doses, use a volume of 20 mL per site and an infusion rate of 15–20 mL/hour per site.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10% may be administered by sub-Q infusion for treatment of primary immunodeficiency.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Also may be administered by IV infusion (see IV Administration of Gammaked 10% under Dosage and Administration).<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Administer Hizentra 20% only by sub-Q infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Prefilled syringes and vials are for single use only and should not be shaken;<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> discard partially used syringes and vials.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Make sub-Q infusions into the abdomen, thighs, upper arms, and/or lateral hips using an infusion pump.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

CIDP: For initial sub-Q infusions of Hizentra 20%, use a maximum volume of 20 mL at each infusion site and a maximum infusion rate of 20 mL/hour at each infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> For subsequent infusions, the volume may be increased up to 50 mL at each infusion site and infusion rate may be increased up to a maximum of 50 mL/hour at each infusion site as tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia is commercially available as a kit containing a vial of immune globulin subcutaneous 10% copackaged with a vial of recombinant human hyaluronidase.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Administer both components only by sub-Q infusion sequentially at same infusion site.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

For each dose of Hyqvia, administer entire contents of vial containing recombinant human hyaluronidase component (acts locally to temporarily increase permeability of sub-Q tissue to increase dispersion and absorption of the immune globulin component) first.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Within approximately 10 minutes after completion of sub-Q infusion of recombinant human hyaluronidase component, administer appropriate dose of the immune globulin subcutaneous 10% component using same sub-Q infusion site and same needle set.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Do not mix recombinant human hyaluronidase component and immune globulin subcutaneous 10% component together in same container;<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> do not mix or administer the individual components with other drugs or infusion fluids.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

May be self-administered in the home or other appropriate setting;<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> provide patient and/or their caregiver with instructions and training regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Make sub-Q infusions into the abdomen and/or thighs using an infusion pump.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Avoid bony prominences or scarred, infected, or inflamed areas.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

In patients weighing ≥40 kg, maximum volume at each sub-Q infusion site is 600 mL.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> In patients weighing <40 kg, maximum volume at each site is 300 mL.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Depending on total volume required and tolerability, each dose of immune globulin subcutaneous 10% may be divided and administered using 2 infusion sites on opposite sides of the body.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> When 2 sites are used, also divide the dose of recombinant human hyaluronidase and administer half at each site.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Rotate administration sites on opposite sides of the body between successive infusions.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Consult manufacturer’s instructions provided with Hyqvia and with the infusion pump for specific information regarding sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Recombinant human hyaluronidase component of Hyqvia: Administer sub-Q at an infusion rate of 1–2 mL/minute or as tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Immune globulin subcutaneous 10% component of Hyqvia: Administer first 4 or 5 sub-Q infusions using increasing infusion rate and a variable infusion rate (ramp-up period).<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Adjust time intervals and number of rate changes if full dose and maximum rate are tolerated.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Consult manufacturer’s instructions provided with Hyqvia for specific information on recommended sub-Q infusion rates and time intervals during the ramp-up period.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Dosage

Children†: Single dose of 0.1 or 0.2 mL/kg of IGIM in those staying in such areas for up to 1 or 2 months, respectively.<html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> If period of exposure in such areas will be ≥2 months, give 0.2 mL/kg once every 2 months.<html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

Primary immunization with an age-appropriate schedule of hepatitis A vaccine before an expected exposure to HAV is preferred in children and infants ≥12 months of age, unless contraindicated.<html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

To ensure protection in travelers who are immunocompromised or have chronic liver disease or other chronic medical conditions and plan to depart within 2 weeks, give single dose of IGIM simultaneously with initial dose of hepatitis A vaccine (using different syringes and different injection sites).<html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html>

The above IGIM dosage is higher than previously recommended.<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> This change was made in 2017 based on data indicating that HAV IgG antibody (anti-HAV IgG) potency of currently available IGIM is lower than in the past (most likely because decreasing prevalence of previous HAV infection among plasma donors resulted in lower anti-HAV antibody levels in donor plasma).<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

Infants <12 months of age†, immunocompromised individuals, individuals with chronic liver disease, and whenever hepatitis A vaccine is contraindicated: Give single dose of 0.1 mL/kg of IGIM as soon as possible after exposure (ideally within 2 weeks).<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

Individuals ≥12 months of age: ACIP, CDC, and AAP prefer active immunization with an age-appropriate schedule of hepatitis A vaccine since it provides long-term protection.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

In individuals receiving IGIM for HAV postexposure prophylaxis and in whom hepatitis A vaccine also recommended for other reasons, give single dose of IGIM concurrently with first dose of hepatitis A vaccine (using different syringes and different injection sites).<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

Efficacy of IGIM for HAV postexposure prophylaxis not established if given >2 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>115</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

The above IGIM dosage is higher than previously recommended.<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> This change was made in 2017 based on data indicating that HAV IgG antibody (anti-HAV IgG) potency of currently available IGIM is lower than in the past (most likely because decreasing prevalence of previous HAV infection among plasma donors resulted in lower anti-HAV antibody levels in donor plasma).<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

Manufacturer recommends single dose of 0.25 mL/kg of IGIM given within 6 days after exposure in susceptible individuals.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> If susceptible child is immunocompromised, manufacturer recommends single dose of 0.5 mL/kg (up to 15 mL) given immediately after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

ACIP and AAP recommend single dose of 0.5 mL/kg (up to 15 mL) of IGIM given within 6 days after exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html> ACIP states optimal dose needed to provide protection against measles unknown.<html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html>

Individuals ≥12 months of age: Initiate active immunization with a vaccine containing measles virus vaccine live (e.g., MMR) 6 months after the IGIM dose, unless the vaccine is contraindicated.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html> (See Specific Drugs and Laboratory Tests under Interactions.)

Individuals currently receiving immune globulin therapy who received IGIV (≥400 mg/kg) within 3 weeks prior to measles exposure or received immune globulin subcutaneous (≥200 mg/kg) for 2 consecutive weeks prior to measles exposure should be sufficiently protected against measles.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10% (children ≥2 years of age): If patient is already receiving a dosage <400 mg/kg once every 3–4 weeks and is at risk of measles exposure (i.e., susceptible traveler to measles endemic area), give a dose of at least 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) just prior to expected measles exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> If a susceptible individual has been exposed to measles, give a dose of 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) as soon as possible after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10% (children ≥2 years of age): If patient is already receiving a dosage <400 mg/kg once every 3–4 weeks and is at risk of measles exposure (i.e., susceptible traveler to measles endemic area), give a dose of at least 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) just prior to measles exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> If a susceptible individual has been exposed to measles, give a dose of 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) as soon as possible after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

Octagam 5%: If patient is already receiving a dosage <400 mg/kg once every 3–4 weeks and is at risk of measles exposure (i.e., susceptible traveler to measles endemic area, measles outbreak in US), increase dosage to at least 400 mg/kg just prior to measles exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> If a susceptible individual has been exposed to measles, give a dose of 400 mg/kg as soon as possible after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20% (children ≥2 years of age): Use minimum total weekly dose of 200 mg/kg for 2 consecutive weeks in those at risk of measles exposure (e.g., susceptible traveler to measles endemic area, measles outbreak in US).<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If a biweekly regimen is being used, give a single dose of at least 400 mg/kg.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If a susceptible individual has been exposed to measles, give a dose of at least 400 mg/kg as soon as possible after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Manufacturer recommends single dose of 0.6–1.2 mL/kg of IGIM given promptly.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

IGIV (not IGIM) usually recommended when VZIG unavailable.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>156</sup></body></html> (See Varicella under Uses.)

Carimune NF: For induction therapy, usual dosage is 400 mg/kg IV once daily for 2–5 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> For treatment of acute childhood ITP, if an initial platelet count response to first 2 doses is adequate (30,000–50,000/mm3), discontinue therapy after second day of the 5-day regimen.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> For treatment of chronic ITP, if platelet count decreases to <30,000/mm3 and/or clinically important bleeding becomes apparent following initial induction therapy, administer 400 mg/kg as a single maintenance infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> If adequate response does not occur, increase maintenance dose to 800–1000 mg/kg given as a single infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

Privigen 10% (adolescents ≥15 years of age): 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg) for chronic ITP.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Carefully consider potential benefits versus risks before using this high-dose regimen in patients at increased risk of thrombosis, hemolysis, acute kidney injury, or volume overload.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

For initial treatment of acute phase, AAP, AHA, and ACCP recommend a single dose of 2 g/kg of IGIV given by IV infusion (usually over 10–12 hours) as soon as possible (optimally within 7–10 days of disease onset).<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>300</sup></body></html> Used in conjunction with appropriate aspirin therapy (e.g., 80–100 mg/kg daily continued for up to 14 days and/or until patient has been afebrile for 48–72 hours; may be followed by low-dose aspirin therapy).<html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>300</sup></body></html>

If no response (i.e., fever persists or recurs ≥36 hours after the IGIV dose), AHA and AAP state that retreatment with a second IGIV dose of 2 g/kg and continued aspirin therapy is a reasonable option.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> Use of additional or alternative anti-inflammatory or immunosuppressive agents may be necessary in IGIV-resistant patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> Consult specialized references for additional information on management of such individuals.<html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html>

Gammagard S/D (IgA <1 mcg/mL): Manufacturer recommends a single dose of 1 g/kg IV beginning within 7 days of onset of fever or, alternatively, 400 mg/kg once daily for 4 consecutive days beginning within 7 days of onset of fever.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Used in conjunction with appropriate aspirin therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

In one study evaluating IGIV and aspirin therapy, a single 2-g/kg IGIV dose was as effective or more effective in preventing coronary artery abnormalities than a 4-day regimen (400 mg/kg daily for 4 days),<html><head></head><body><sup>240</sup></body></html> and the single IGIV dose was associated with more rapid defervescence, shorter duration of fever, and more rapid return to normal of clinical measures of inflammation.<html><head></head><body><sup>240</sup></body></html>

Cutaquig 16.5%: If patient with primary immunodeficiency is at risk of measles exposure and is receiving a weekly dosage <245 mg/kg, manufacturer states the weekly dosage should be increased to ≥245 mg/kg.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20%: If patient with primary immunodeficiency is at risk of measles exposure (e.g., susceptible traveler to measles endemic area, measles outbreak in US), manufacturer recommends minimum total weekly dose of 200 mg/kg for 2 consecutive weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If a biweekly sub-Q regimen is being used, give a single dose of at least 400 mg/kg.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If a susceptible individual has been exposed to measles, give a dose of at least 400 mg/kg as soon as possible after the exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Manufacturer recommends single dose of 0.55 mL/kg of IGIM to modify rubella in susceptible pregnant women exposed to the disease.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> Routine use not recommended.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>131</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> (See Rubella under Uses.)

Manufacturer recommends single dose of 0.6–1.2 mL/kg of IGIM given promptly.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

IGIV (not IGIM) usually recommended when VZIG is unavailable.<html><head></head><body><sup>156</sup></body></html>

Single dose of 400 mg/kg of IGIV (ideally within 96 hours after varicella exposure).<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>156</sup></body></html>

May not be necessary in patients already receiving immune globulin replacement therapy with IGIV (≥400 mg/kg given at regular intervals) if the last dose was administered within 3 weeks prior to varicella exposure.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>146</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>155</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>156</sup></body></html>

Minimum serum IgG concentration necessary for protection varies among patients;<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> there is considerable interindividual variation in half-life of IgG in patients with primary humoral immunodeficiency.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> Monitor clinical response and adjust IGIV dosage to achieve desired trough serum IgG concentrations and/or clinical response.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

Individuals with primary immunodeficiency who are exposed to measles or are at increased risk of measles exposure: Some manufacturers state it may be prudent to administer an extra IGIV dose or increase the IGIV dose, respectively.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> ACIP and AAP state that those currently receiving immune globulin replacement therapy who received an IGIV dose of ≥400 mg/kg within 3 weeks prior to measles exposure or received immune globulin subcutaneous in a dosage of ≥200 mg/kg for 2 consecutive weeks prior to measles exposure should be sufficiently protected against measles.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html>

Asceniv 10%: 300–800 mg/kg IV once every 3–4 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> Starting with second infusion, adjust dosage proportionately, targeting a trough IgG concentration of ≥600 mg/dL.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> Dosage adjustment may be required in those who fail to maintain trough serum IgG concentrations ≥500 mg/dL with a target of 600 mg/dL.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html>

Bivigam 10%: 300–800 mg/kg IV once every 3–4 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> Starting with second infusion, adjust dosage over time to achieve and maintain trough serum IgG concentrations >600 mg/dL.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> If trough serum IgG concentrations cannot be maintained at ≥500 mg/dL, adjust dosage to achieve a target trough serum IgG concentration of 600 mg/dL.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html>

Monitor clinical response and individualize dosage of immune globulin subcutaneous based on clinical response and trough serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Individuals with primary immunodeficiency who are exposed to measles: ACIP states that those currently receiving immune globulin replacement therapy who received an IGIV dose of ≥400 mg/kg within 3 weeks prior to measles exposure or received immune globulin subcutaneous in a dosage ≥200 mg/kg for 2 consecutive weeks prior to measles exposure should be sufficiently protected against measles.<html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html>

Cutaquig 16.5%: Administer sub-Q once weekly.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> When switching from IGIV or a different immune globulin subcutaneous preparation, initiate in those who have received ≥3 months of prior treatment and give first dose of Cutaquig 16.5% 1 week after last dose of prior immune globulin.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Calculate initial dose of Cutaquig 16.5% based on prior immune globulin dosage.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information regarding initial and subsequent dosage of Cutaquig 16.5%.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Cuvitru 20%: Give at regular intervals ranging from once daily up to once every 2 weeks (biweekly).<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Calculate initial sub-Q dose based on monthly dose of prior immune globulin regimen.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> If switching from IGIV or immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase (Hyqvia), give initial dose 1 week after last dose of the other immune globulin.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information regarding initial and subsequent dosage for sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Gammagard Liquid 10%: Administer sub-Q once weekly.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Give initial dose approximately 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> To calculate initial sub-Q weekly dose, divide patient’s previous IGIV dose (in g) by the number of weeks between IGIV doses (i.e., divide by 3 or 4 depending on whether patient was receiving IGIV every 3 or 4 weeks), then multiply this value by a dose adjustment factor of 1.37.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Base maintenance sub-Q doses on clinical response and target trough IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information on how to adjust sub-Q dosage based on trough serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10%: Administer sub-Q once weekly.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Give initial dose 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> To calculate initial sub-Q weekly dose, divide patient’s previous IGIV dose (in g) by the number of weeks between IGIV doses (i.e., divide by 3 or 4 depending on whether the patient was receiving IGIV every 3 or 4 weeks), then multiply this value by a dose adjustment factor of 1.37.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Adjust weekly sub-Q dose over time to achieve desired trough serum IgG concentrations and clinical response.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information on how to adjust sub-Q dosage based on trough serum IgG concentrations and for information regarding dosage requirements for patients switching from another immune globulin subcutaneous preparation to Gammaked 10%.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10%: Administer sub-Q once weekly.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Give initial dose 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> To calculate initial sub-Q weekly dose, divide patient’s previous IGIV dose (in g) by the number of weeks between IGIV doses (i.e., divide by 3 or 4 depending on whether the patient was receiving IGIV every 3 or 4 weeks), then multiply this value by a dose adjustment factor of 1.37.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Adjust weekly sub-Q dose over time to achieve desired trough serum IgG concentrations and clinical response.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information regarding initial and subsequent dosage for sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20%: Administer sub-Q at regular intervals ranging from once daily up to once every 2 weeks (biweekly).<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Use only in patients who have been receiving IGIV for ≥3 months before being switched to Hizentra 20%;<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> give initial dose 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information regarding initial and subsequent dosage for sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia (immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase): Administer sub-Q once every 3 to 4 weeks after an initial ramp-up period that incrementally changes the dosage regimen from a 1-week regimen to a 3- or 4-week regimen and allows the patient to become accustomed to the large volumes required for a full monthly dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer's literature for specific information on the ramp-up schedule, including specific doses and dosing intervals for sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Xembify 20%: Administer sub-Q once weekly;<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> alternatively, may divide weekly dose and give in 2–7 doses during the week.<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> When switching from IGIV, calculate initial weekly dose of Xembify 20% based on previous IGIV monthly (or every 3 weeks) dosage and give first dose of Xembify 20% 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> When switching from a different immune globulin subcutaneous preparation, initial weekly dose of Xembify 20% should be the same as weekly dose of prior immune globulin subcutaneous treatment.<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> Base subsequent doses on clinical response and target trough IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> Consult manufacturer’s literature for specific information regarding how to adjust sub-Q dosage based on trough serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Carimune NF: For induction therapy, usual dosage is 400 mg/kg IV once daily for 2–5 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> If platelet count decreases to <30,000/mm3 and/or clinically important bleeding becomes apparent following initial induction therapy, administer 400 mg/kg as a single maintenance infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> If adequate response does not occur, increase maintenance dose to 800–1000 mg/kg given as a single infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

Flebogamma 10% DIF: 1 g/kg IV once daily for 2 consecutive days for chronic ITP.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Gammagard S/D (IgA <1 mcg/mL): Single dose of 1 g/kg IV for chronic ITP.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Determine need for additional doses based on clinical response and platelet count.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> If required, up to 3 doses may be given on alternate days.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10%: 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg);<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> if increase in platelet count adequate 24 hours after first dose, second dose may be withheld.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Alternatively, give 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) once daily for 5 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> High-dose regimen (1 g/kg for 1 or 2 doses) not recommended in patients with expanded fluid volumes or when fluid volume may be a concern.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 5%: 1 g/kg (20 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> Carefully consider risks and benefits of this high-dose regimen before using in patients at increased risk of thrombosis, hemolysis, acute kidney injury, or volume overload.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> Adequate data not available regarding platelet response to a lower-dose regimen (i.e., 400 mg/kg daily for 5 consecutive days).<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 10%: 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> Carefully consider risks and benefits of this high-dose regimen before using in patients at increased risk of thrombosis, hemolysis, acute kidney injury, or volume overload.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> Adequate data not available regarding platelet response to a lower-dose regimen (i.e., 400 mg/kg daily for 5 consecutive days).<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10%: 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg);<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> if increase in platelet count adequate 24 hours after first dose, second dose may be withheld.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Alternatively, give 400 mg/kg (4 mL/kg) once daily for 5 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> High-dose regimen (1 g/kg for 1 or 2 doses) not recommended in patients with expanded fluid volumes or when fluid volume may be a concern.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

Octagam 10%: For chronic ITP, 1 g/kg IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html>

Panzyga 10%: 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg).<html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

Privigen 10%: 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) IV once daily for 2 consecutive days (total dose 2 g/kg) for chronic ITP.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Carefully consider potential benefits versus risks before using this high-dose regimen in patients at increased risk of thrombosis, hemolysis, acute kidney injury, or volume overload.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Gammagard S/D (IgA <1 mcg/mL): 400 mg/kg IV once every 3–4 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10%: Loading dose of 2 g/kg (20 mL/kg) IV given in divided doses over 2–4 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Then, maintenance dosage of 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) given as a single dose once every 3 weeks or, alternatively, 2 doses of 0.5 g/kg (5 mL/kg) given on 2 consecutive days once every 3 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10%: Loading dose of 2 g/kg (20 mL/kg) IV given in divided doses over 2–4 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Then, maintenance dosage of 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) given as a single dose once every 3 weeks or, alternatively, 2 doses of 0.5 g/kg (5 mL/kg) given on 2 consecutive days once every 3 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Has been continued for up to 48 weeks in clinical studies in patients with CIDP.<html><head></head><body><sup>298</sup></body></html>

Privigen 10%: Loading dose of 2 g/kg (20 mL/kg) IV given in divided doses over 2–5 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Then, maintenance dosage of 1 g/kg (10 mL/kg) given as a single dose once every 3 weeks or, alternatively, as 2 doses given on 2 consecutive days once every 3 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Has not been studied for durations >6 months.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> After response is obtained during initial treatment period, not all patients require indefinite maintenance therapy to remain free of CIDP symptoms.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Assess patient's response and demonstrated need for continued Privigen 10% therapy beyond 6 months.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20% for maintenance treatment to prevent relapse: Give initial dose sub-Q 1 week after last IGIV dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Weekly dosage of Hizentra 20% is 0.2 g/kg (1 mL/kg) given sub-Q in 1 or 2 sessions over 1 or 2 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Clinical study data evaluating use of Hizentra 20% for maintenance therapy in CIDP patients transitioning from IGIV indicate that a weekly dose of 0.4 g/kg (2 mL/kg) also is safe and effective when used to prevent CIDP relapse.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If CIDP symptoms worsen, consider discontinuing Hizentra 20% and reinitiating IGIV.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If improvement and stabilization are observed during IGIV retreatment, consider discontinuing IGIV and reinitiating Hizentra 20% using a weekly dose of 0.4 g/kg sub-Q given in 2 sessions over 1 or 2 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> If CIDP symptoms worsen on the 0.4 g/kg weekly dose, consider discontinuing Hizentra 20% and reinitiating IGIV.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Maintenance therapy with Hizentra 20% has been studied for a duration of 6 months and for an additional 12 months of follow-up.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Use for maintenance therapy for a longer duration should be individualized based on patient's response and need for continued therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Although optimum dosage not established, if IGIV used when disability is severe enough to warrant treatment, the European Federation of Neurological Societies (EFNS) and Peripheral Nerve Society (PNS) suggest an initial IGIV dosage of 2 g/kg given in divided doses over 2–5 consecutive days.<html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>311</sup></body></html> If initial regimen is effective, these clinicians state that maintenance therapy can be considered using 1 g/kg once every 2–4 weeks or 2 g/kg every 1–2 months;<html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>311</sup></body></html> frequency of maintenance therapy should be guided by response.<html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>311</sup></body></html>

Gammagard Liquid 10%: Manufacturer recommends maintenance dosage ranging from 500 mg/kg to 2.4 g/kg IV once every month.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Adjust dosage to achieve desired clinical response and avoid worsening of muscle weakness.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Although safety and efficacy and optimum dosage not established,<html><head></head><body><sup>312</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>317</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>318</sup></body></html> EFNS and others recommend 0.4 g/kg of IGIV daily for 5 days.<html><head></head><body><sup>301</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>312</sup></body></html> Unclear whether IGIV is effective when initiated more than 2 weeks after symptom onset.<html><head></head><body><sup>317</sup></body></html>

If relapse occurs after an initial response, EFNS states that retreatment with a dosage of 2 g/kg of IGIV given in divided doses over 2–5 consecutive days can be considered.<html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> Retreatment also can be considered in those who do not respond to initial regimen,<html><head></head><body><sup>310</sup></body></html> but other clinicians state it is unclear whether retreatment is beneficial in such patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>305</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>318</sup></body></html>

Patients with severe hypogammaglobulinemia (IgG <400 mg/dL) within the first 100 days after allogeneic HSCT†: 500 mg/kg of IGIV once weekly has been used.<html><head></head><body><sup>262</sup></body></html>

Individualize dosage to maintain trough serum IgG concentrations exceeding 400–500 mg/dL; monitor trough serum IgG concentrations regularly (e.g., approximately every 2 weeks).<html><head></head><body><sup>262</sup></body></html>

200–400 mg/kg of IGIV has been recommended as an alternative when TIG not available.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> (See Tetanus under Uses.)

150–400 mg/kg of IGIV once daily for 5 days or, alternatively, a single dose of 1–2 g/kg has been used.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> Optimal dosage regimen not established.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html>

Prescribing Limits

Maximum single IGIM dose: 15 mL.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

Maximum single IGIM dose: 15 mL.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

Special Populations

IGIV: Reduce dose, concentration, and/or rate of administration; maximum safe dose, concentration, and rate of administration not established.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> Ensure that patients are not volume depleted and are well hydrated; administer at the minimum concentration available and minimum infusion rate practicable.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> (See Renal Effects under Cautions and see IV Administration under Dosage and Administration.)

Warnings/Precautions

Thrombotic events (e.g., chest pain, MI, CHF, cerebral infarction, ischemic encephalopathy, severe headache requiring hospitalization, pulmonary embolism, retinal vein occlusion, peripheral venous thrombosis), including some fatalities, reported in patients receiving immune globulin.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>252</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>253</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>254</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>255</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>256</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>257</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>258</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>259</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>328</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>329</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Etiology for thrombosis in patients receiving immune globulin not fully determined;<html><head></head><body><sup>252</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>253</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>255</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>256</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>259</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>260</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>329</sup></body></html> immune globulin-induced alterations of blood rheology (e.g., platelet activation, increased blood viscosity, elevated levels of activated coagulation factor XI [XIa]) and infusion-related hypertensive effects appear to contribute to development of thrombotic complications.<html><head></head><body><sup>252</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>253</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>256</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>260</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>329</sup></body></html>

Patients at risk for thrombotic events may include those with a history of atherosclerosis, cardiovascular risk factors, impaired cardiac output, coagulation or hypercoagulable disorders (e.g., factor V Leiden), prolonged periods of immobilization, advanced age, acquired or inherited thrombotic disorder, previous thrombotic or thromboembolic event, known or suspected hyperviscosity, indwelling central vascular catheters, and/or treatment with estrogen-containing preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> Weigh potential risks and benefits of immune globulin against those of alternative therapies in all patients in whom immune globulin is being considered.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html>

Prior to immune globulin therapy, carefully evaluate patients with thrombotic risk factors (e.g., those with a history of atherosclerosis, cardiovascular risk factors, impaired cardiac output, coagulation or hypercoagulable disorders [e.g., factor V Leiden], prolonged periods of immobilization, advanced age, acquired or inherited thrombotic disorder, history of venous or arterial thrombosis, known or suspected hyperviscosity, indwelling central vascular catheters, and/or treatment with estrogen-containing preparations).<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>252</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>253</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>255</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>256</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>257</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>259</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>260</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>328</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>329</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

In patients at risk for thrombosis, use minimum dose and minimum infusion rate practicable and monitor closely for signs and symptoms of
