Because of potential increased risk of thrombosis, consider baseline assessment of blood viscosity in patients at risk for hyperviscosity (e.g., those with cryoglobulins, fasting chylomicronemia/markedly high triacylglycerols [triglycerides], or monoclonal gammopathies).<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>328</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>329</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Renal dysfunction, acute renal failure, osmotic nephrosis, and death reported in patients receiving immune globulin.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>251</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Patients at increased risk for acute renal failure include, but are not limited to, those with any degree of preexisting renal insufficiency, diabetes mellitus, volume depletion, sepsis, or paraproteinemia; those receiving concomitant nephrotoxic drugs; and/or those >65 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

IGIV preparations stabilized with sucrose (e.g., Carimune NF) have been associated with renal dysfunction more frequently than other IGIV preparations;<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> weigh benefits of these preparations against potential risk of renal dysfunction.<html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> Maximum infusion rate of 3 mg of sucrose/kg per minute recommended.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>261</sup></body></html>

To reduce risk of acute renal failure, ensure that patients are not volume depleted and are adequately hydrated prior to administration of IGIV or immune globulin subcutaneous and use lowest effective dosage.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>251</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Administer IGIV or immune globulin subcutaneous at the minimum concentration available and the minimum infusion rate practicable, especially in patients at increased risk for acute renal failure.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Assess urine output and renal function (BUN, Scr) prior to and at appropriate intervals during therapy with IGIV or immune globulin subcutaneous, especially in patients considered at increased risk for acute renal failure.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

If renal dysfunction occurs, consider discontinuing immune globulin therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Increased risk of infusion reactions (e.g., fever, chills, nausea, vomiting) when immune globulin administered by IV or sub-Q infusion in patients who have not previously received immune globulin therapy, in patients being switched to a different immune globulin preparation, and in those who have not received immune globulin within the preceding 8 weeks.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

IGIV may cause a precipitous fall in BP and clinical manifestations of anaphylaxis, which appear to be related to the rate of IGIV infusion; do not exceed the recommended rate of infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> These reactions generally appear 0.5–1 hour after initiation of the infusion and include facial flushing, chest tightness, chills, fever, dizziness, nausea, vomiting, diaphoresis, and hypotension or hypertension.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

Hypertensive urgency with elevated systolic BP (≥180 mm Hg) and/or elevated diastolic BP (≥120 mm Hg) reported during and/or shortly following infusion of IGIV (Privigen 10%).<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> BP elevations were reported more often among patients with a history of hypertension and resolved or significantly improved within hours with either observation alone or changes in oral antihypertensive therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Closely monitor for adverse reactions throughout the infusion<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> since these reactions may rarely lead to shock.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

If flushing, changes in BP or pulse, or other infusion reactions occur, slow or temporarily stop the infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> In some cases when symptoms subside promptly, the infusion may be resumed at a rate that is comfortable for the patient.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Stop infusion immediately if anaphylaxis or other severe reactions occur.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> (See Sensitivity Reactions under Cautions.)

Severe hypersensitivity reactions, including anaphylaxis, reported rarely following administration of IGIV, IGIM, or immune globulin subcutaneous.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

If a severe hypersensitivity reaction occurs, discontinue immune globulin immediately and institute appropriate therapy as indicated.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> Epinephrine and antihistamines should be readily available in case anaphylaxis or an anaphylactoid reaction occurs.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Use IGIM with caution in patients with a history of systemic allergic reactions to immune globulin preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

The manufacturer of IGIM states that intradermal sensitivity testing should not be performed;<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> intradermal injection of concentrated buffered immune globulin solution frequently causes localized chemical irritation, which may be misinterpreted as evidence of hypersensitivity and result in needed therapy being withheld.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

IGIM, IGIV, and immune globulin subcutaneous should not be used in IgA-deficient individuals with antibodies against IgA and a history of hypersensitivity.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Individuals with selective IgA deficiency or individuals in whom IgA deficiency exists as a component of an immunodeficiency disease may have serum antibodies to IgA or may develop such antibodies following administration of immune globulin or other blood products containing IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> Potential for severe hypersensitivity (e.g., anaphylactic) reactions to IgA in such patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Administer only in a setting where supportive care is available for treating life-threatening reactions.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> If a hypersensitivity reaction occurs, consider alternative therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

All commercially available preparations of IGIV contain trace amounts of IgA, but the amount varies among the different preparations.<html><head></head><body><sup>262</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Concentration of IgA that will not provoke a reaction to IgA not known.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Asceniv 10%: ≤200 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html>

Bivigam 10%: ≤200 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html>

Carimune NF: Trace amounts of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

Cutaquig 16.5% : ≤600 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Cuvitru 20%: Average of 80 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Flebogamma 5% DIF: <50 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Flebogamma 10% DIF: <32 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Gammagard Liquid 10%: Average of 37 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Gammagard S/D: <1 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10%: Average of 46 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 5%: Trace amounts of IgA (<10 mcg/mL).<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 10%: Trace amounts of IgA (<20 mcg/mL).<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10%: Average of 46 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20%: ≤50 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia 10%: Average of 37 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Octagam 5%: ≤200 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html>

Octagam 10%: Average of 106 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html>

Panzyga 10%: Average of 100 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

Privigen 10%: ≤25 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Xembify 20%: Contains IgA (amount not specified).<html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Octagam 5% and Octagam 10% contain maltose, a disaccharide sugar derived from corn.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> Hypersensitivity reactions may occur if these preparations are used in patients with corn allergy.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> Manufacturer states avoid Octagam 5% in patients with known corn allergies;<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> contraindicated in those with acute hypersensitivity reactions to corn.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html>

IGIV and immune globulin subcutaneous may contain blood group antibodies that can act as hemolysins and induce in vivo coating of RBCs with immunoglobulin, causing a positive direct antiglobulin reaction and, rarely, hemolysis.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Delayed hemolytic anemia can develop subsequent to immune globulin therapy due to enhanced RBC sequestration, and acute hemolysis consistent with intravascular hemolysis has been reported.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Monitor for clinical signs and symptoms of hemolysis (e.g., increased heart rate, swelling, fatigue, difficulty breathing, yellowing of skin or eyes, dark-colored urine).<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

In higher risk patients, consider performing appropriate laboratory testing (e.g., hemoglobin or hematocrit) prior to IGIV infusion and within approximately 36–96 hours after infusion.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> If clinical signs and symptoms of hemolysis or a significant drop in hemoglobin or hematocrit occur, perform additional confirmatory laboratory tests.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

If a blood transfusion is indicated for a patient who developed hemolysis with clinically compromising anemia after receiving immune globulin, adequate cross-matching should be performed to avoid exacerbating on-going hemolysis.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

Monitor patients receiving immune globulin for adverse pulmonary reactions.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Hyperproteinemia, increased serum viscosity, and hyponatremia may occur in patients receiving IGIV.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> The hyponatremia is likely to be pseudohyponatremia, as demonstrated by decreased calculated serum osmolality or elevated osmolar gap.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

If hyponatremia occurs, it is critical to distinguish true hyponatremia from pseudohyponatremia.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> Treatment aimed at decreasing serum free water in patients with pseudohyponatremia may lead to volume depletion, a further increase in serum viscosity, and may predispose to thromboembolic events.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> (See Thrombosis under Cautions.)

Gammagard S/D (IgA <1 mcg/mL) contains approximately 8.5 mg of sodium chloride per mL;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> consider this amount when determining dietary sodium in patients on a low-sodium diet since hypernatremia may occur.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Because of risk of volume overload, manufacturers of Gammaplex 5%, Gammaplex 10%, and Privigen 10% state carefully consider relative risks and benefits before using high-dose IGIV regimens (1 g/kg daily for 1–2 days) for treatment of chronic ITP in patients at increased risk of volume overload.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

Manufacturers of Gammaked 10% and Gamunex-C 10% state high-dose IGIV regimens (1 g/kg daily for 1–2 days) not recommended for treatment of chronic ITP in individuals with expanded fluid volumes or when fluid volume may be a concern.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Because immune globulin preparations are prepared from pooled human plasma, they may carry a risk of transmitting human viruses (e.g., HAV, HBV, HCV, HIV) and theoretically may carry a risk of transmitting the causative agents of Creutzfeldt-Jakob disease (CJD) or variant CJD (vCJD).<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>210</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Risk for transmission of recognized blood-borne viruses is considered to be low because plasma donors are screened for certain viruses (HBV, HCV, HIV, human parvovirus [B19V]) and viral reduction/inactivation procedures used in immune globulin production reduce the risk of transmission.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> Report all infections thought possibly to have been transmitted by immune globulin preparations to the appropriate manufacturer.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>227</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia (immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase): In clinical studies, nonneutralizing antibodies to recombinant human hyaluronidase developed in 18% of patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Clinical importance unknown.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Animal studies indicate that antibodies to recombinant human hyaluronidase cross the placenta and are transferred to offspring during lactation.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> These antibodies could potentially cross-react with endogenous human hyaluronidase (expressed in adult male testes, epididymis, and sperm).<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Immune globulin preparations that contain maltose (e.g., Cutaquig 16.5%, Octagam 5%, Octagam 10%) may cause falsely elevated results in blood glucose determinations with tests that use nonspecific methods based on glucose dehydrogenase pyrroloquinolinequinone (GDH-PQQ) or glucose-dye oxidoreductase.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> (See Specific Drugs and Laboratory Tests under Interactions.)

Animal reproduction studies not performed with IGIM, IGIV, or immune globulin subcutaneous, and it is not known whether immune globulins can cause fetal harm when administered to pregnant women.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Some manufacturers state use immune globulin during pregnancy only when clearly needed.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

ACIP states there are no known risks associated with immune globulins used for passive immunization in pregnant women.<html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia (immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase): Some patients receiving this preparation have developed antibodies to recombinant human hyaluronidase and these antibodies potentially could cross-react with endogenous human hyaluronidase, which is expressed in adult male testes, epididymis, and sperm.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Not known whether these anti-recombinant human hyaluronidase antibodies interfere with human fertility.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Not evaluated in nursing women.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Not known whether immune globulin is distributed into milk following IM, IV, or sub-Q administration, affects milk production, or affects the breast-fed infant.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>281</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Use with caution in nursing women.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Consider benefits of breast-feeding and importance of immune globulin to the woman as well as potential adverse effects on breast-fed infant from the drug or from underlying maternal condition.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia (immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase): Animal studies indicate maternal antibodies bound to recombinant human hyaluronidase are transferred to nursing offspring;<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> no adverse effects on pregnancy or offspring development associated with these antibodies reported.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Data not available regarding use in nursing women;<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> possible effects of antibodies to recombinant human hyaluronidase that may be transferred to infants unknown.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

GamaSTAN: Manufacturer states safety and efficacy of IGIM not established in pediatric patients;<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> however, passive immunization with IGIM is recommended by ACIP and AAP in pediatric patients under certain circumstances using same dosages recommended for adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>133</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>231</sup></body></html> (See Hepatitis A Virus [HAV]) Infection [Preexposure Prophylaxis], Hepatitis A Virus [HAV] Infection [Postexposure Prophylaxis], and Measles, under Uses.)

Asceniv 10%: Evaluated in limited number of pediatric patients 6–16 years of age for treatment of primary immunodeficiency;<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> safety, efficacy, and pharmacokinetic profiles in adolescents were comparable to adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> Data insufficient regarding safety, efficacy, and pharmacokinetics in pediatric patients <12 years of age;<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> safety and efficacy not studied in those <3 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html>

Bivigam 10%: Safety and efficacy not established in children <6 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> Only limited data regarding efficacy and safety in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html>

Carimune NF: Studies using high doses in pediatric patients with acute or chronic ITP did not reveal any specific differences in safety in pediatric patients versus adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

Cutaquig 16.5%: Only limited number of pediatric patients were included in clinical study evaluating use for treatment of primary immunodeficiency.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established in pediatric patients <17 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Cuvitru 20%: Safety and efficacy not established in pediatric patients <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Flebogamma 5% DIF: Safety and efficacy not established in pediatric patients <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

Flebogamma 10% DIF: Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of primary immunodeficiency in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> Evaluated in a limited number of children and adolescents with chronic ITP;<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> safety and efficacy not established for treatment of chronic ITP in children <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

Gammagard Liquid 10%: Safety and efficacy for treatment of primary immunodeficiency not established in children <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy for treatment of MMN not established in pediatric patients of any age.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Gammagard S/D (IgA <1 mcg/mL): Clinical studies in patients with primary immunodeficiency did not include sufficient numbers of pediatric patients ≤16 years of age to determine whether they respond differently than adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of ITP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy established for treatment of Kawasaki disease in pediatric patients;<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> majority of patients in clinical studies were <5 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Gammaked 10%: Safety and efficacy of IV route established for treatment of primary immunodeficiency in pediatric patients;<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> safety and efficacy of sub-Q route not established for treatment of primary immunodeficiency in pediatric patients <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy of IV (not sub-Q) route established for treatment of ITP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of CIDP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 5%: Safety and efficacy for treatment of primary immunodeficiency not established in children <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> Clinical studies in patients with ITP included only limited number of children;<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> data insufficient to determine whether efficacy in pediatric patients with ITP differs from that in adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html>

Gammaplex 10%: Evaluated in limited number of pediatric patients 3–15 years of age for treatment of primary immunodeficiency;<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> pediatric-specific dosage not required to achieve desired serum IgG concentrations in this age group.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> Safety and pharmacokinetics in pediatric patients ≥3 years of age similar to adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of ITP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

Gamunex-C 10%: Safety and efficacy of IV route established for treatment of primary immunodeficiency in pediatric patients;<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> safety and efficacy of sub-Q route not established for treatment of primary immunodeficiency in pediatric patients <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy of IV (not sub-Q) route established for treatment of ITP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of CIDP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

Hizentra 20%: Safety and efficacy for treatment of primary immunodeficiency not established in pediatric patients <2 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy established for replacement therapy in pediatric patients 2–16 years of age with primary immunodeficiency;<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> no differences in safety and efficacy profiles in pediatric patients compared with adults;<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> pediatric-specific dosage not required to achieve desired serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of CIDP in pediatric patients <18 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Hyqvia 10%: Safety not established in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Octagam 5%: Evaluated in a limited number of children 6–16 years of age;<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> no apparent differences in pharmacokinetics, efficacy, or safety compared with adults.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> Pediatric-specific dosage not required to achieve desired serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html>

Octagam 10%: Safety and efficacy not established in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html>

Panzyga 10%: Evaluated in limited number of pediatric patients 2–15 years of age for treatment of primary immunodeficiency.<html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> Pharmacokinetics, efficacy, and safety in these pediatric patients similar to adults; pediatric-specific dosage not required to achieve targeted serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of ITP in pediatric patients.<html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html>

Privigen 10%: Safety and efficacy for treatment of primary immunodeficiency not established in pediatric patients <3 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Has been evaluated in a limited number of children and adolescents with primary immunodeficiency;<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> no apparent differences in safety and efficacy compared with adults; pediatric-specific dosage not required to achieve desired serum IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of chronic ITP in pediatric patients <15 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> Safety and efficacy not established for treatment of CIDP in pediatric patients <18 years of age.<html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Interactions for Immune Globulin

Live Vaccines

Antibodies present in immune globulin preparations may interfere with immune response to some live virus vaccines, including MMR and varicella virus vaccine live;<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> no evidence of interference with immune responses to influenza virus vaccine live intranasal, rotavirus vaccine live oral, typhoid vaccine live oral, yellow fever virus vaccine live, zoster vaccine live, or poliovirus vaccine live oral (OPV; no longer commercially available in US).<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> (See Specific Drugs and Laboratory Tests under Interactions.)

Inactivated Vaccines and Toxoids

ACIP and AAP state that administration of inactivated vaccines and toxoids simultaneously with (at different sites) or at any interval before or after administration of immune globulin preparations should not have clinically important effects on immune responses to the vaccines or toxoids.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Specific Drugs and Laboratory Tests

Drug or Test

Interaction

Comments

Hepatitis A virus vaccine inactivated

Anti-HAV antibody passively acquired from immune globulin may decrease the immune response and antibody concentrations stimulated by the vaccine, but seroconversion rates not affected;<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>195</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>208</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>289</sup></body></html> effect of reduced antibody concentrations on long-term protection against HAV unknown<html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

May administer simultaneously at separate sites using different syringes<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>194</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>195</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>208</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>289</sup></body></html>

Influenza virus vaccine live intranasal

No evidence that immune globulin preparations interfere with immune response to the vaccine<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

May be given simultaneously with or at any interval before or after immune globulin<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Measles, mumps, rubella, and varicella virus vaccines

Antibodies in immune globulin can interfere with immune responses to measles and rubella antigens contained in MMR or MMRV;<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>131</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> effect on immune responses to mumps or varicella antigens unknown<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Duration of interference depends on amount of antigen-specific antibody in the immune globulin preparation<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

MMR, MMRV, or varicella vaccine: Do not administer simultaneously with or for specified intervals before or after administration of immune globulin<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

IGIM: Defer administration of MMR, MMRV, or varicella vaccine for 6 months following IGIM used for HAV preexposure or postexposure prophylaxis<html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html> or for measles prophylaxis in immunocompetent individuals<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

IGIV: Defer administration of MMR, MMRV, or varicella vaccine for 8 months following IGIV used for replacement therapy in patients with primary immunodeficiencies, measles prophylaxis,<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> or varicella postexposure prophylaxis;<html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>269</sup></body></html> defer these vaccines for 8–11 months following IGIV used for treatment of ITP (8 months if IGIV doses were 400 mg/kg or 10–11 months if IGIV doses were ≥800 mg/kg);<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html> defer these vaccines for 11 months following IGIV used for treatment of Kawasaki disease<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

If MMR, MMRV, or varicella vaccine is administered simultaneously (at a separate site) or at an interval shorter than recommended, ACIP and AAP recommend giving an additional vaccine dose after the recommended interval, unless serologic testing is feasible and indicates an adequate antibody response to the vaccine<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Poliovirus vaccine live oral (OPV; no longer commercially available in US)

No evidence that immune globulin preparations interfere with immune response to the vaccine<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html>

May be given simultaneously with or at any interval before or after immune globulin<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html>

Rotavirus vaccine

No evidence that immune globulin preparations interfere with immune response to the vaccine<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>186</sup></body></html>

May be administered simultaneously with or at any time before or after antibody-containing blood products<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Tests, blood glucose (based on glucose dehydrogenase pyrroloquinolinequinone [GDH-PQQ] or glucose-dye oxidoreductase)

Maltose-containing immune globulin preparations (e.g., Cutaquig 16.5%, Octagam): Potential for falsely elevated blood glucose test results<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

May result in inappropriate insulin administration and life-threatening hypoglycemia<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Risk that true cases of hypoglycemia could go untreated if hypoglycemic state is masked by falsely elevated blood glucose determinations<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Use test methods not affected by maltose (e.g., methods that use glucose dehydrogenase nicotine adenine dinucleotide [GDH-NAD], glucose oxidase, or glucose hexokinase) in patients receiving maltose-containing immune globulin preparations<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Tests, fungus

Possible false-positive tests for diagnosis of fungal infection when assay depends on detection of beta-d-glucans;<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> test interference may persist during the weeks following infusion of immune globulin<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Tests, immunohematology (Coombs’ test)

Passively transferred blood group antibodies (e.g., anti-A, anti-B, anti-D) may result in positive direct antiglobulin (Coombs’) test results;<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> possible interference with hematologic studies or transfusion cross-matching procedures<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

Tests, serologic

Patients receiving immune globulin may have passively acquired antibodies that could cause false-positive serologic test results and misinterpretation of these test results<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Typhoid vaccine live oral

No evidence that immune globulin preparations interfere with immune response to the vaccine<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>134</sup></body></html>

Immune Globulin Pharmacokinetics

Absorption

Following IM administration of IGIM, serum concentrations of IgG peak within 2 days.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

Following IV administration of IGIV, there is an immediate post-infusion peak in serum IgG concentrations followed by a biphasic decline.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Following sub-Q administration of immune globulin, peak serum IgG concentrations are lower than those attained with IGIV, but trough concentrations generally are higher.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> In contrast to the biphasic IgG concentrations reported with IGIV, sub-Q immune globulin given once weekly results in relatively stable IgG concentrations.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Peak serum IgG concentrations in patients receiving sub-Q immune globulin generally occur 2.9 days (range: 0–7 days) after a dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

Following sub-Q administration of immune globulin with recombinant human hyaluronidase (Hyqvia), peak serum IgG concentrations are lower than those attained with IGIV, but trough IgG concentrations generally are comparable.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> In addition, AUC of IgG is 20% higher than that attained with immune globulin subcutaneous given without recombinant human hyaluronidase.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Peak serum IgG concentrations in patients receiving Hyqvia generally occur 5 days (range 3.3–5.1 days) after a dose.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Distribution

IgG present in IGIM or IGIV is rapidly and evenly distributed between intravascular and extravascular spaces.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Intact immune globulins cross the placenta in increasing amounts after 30 weeks’ gestation.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

Not known whether immune globulin is distributed into milk following IM, IV, or sub-Q administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>281</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html>

Elimination

IGIV undergoes biphasic elimination;<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> rapid initial decline in serum IgG concentrations associated with equilibration between plasma and extravascular space, followed by slower elimination phase.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

High IgG concentrations and hypermetabolism associated with fever and infection have been reported to coincide with shortened IgG half-life.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

Half-life of IgG in individuals with normal serum IgG concentrations: 18–25 days.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

Half-life of IGIV preparations in patients with immunodeficiencies: 12–59 days.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html>
