Actions

  • Provides a broad spectrum of opsonic and neutralizing IgG antibodies against a wide variety of bacterial and viral agents.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • IgG antibodies contained in immune globulin provide passive immunity by increasing an individual’s antibody titer and antigen-antibody reaction potential and prevent or modify certain infectious diseases in susceptible individuals.<html><head></head><body><sup>105</sup></body></html>

  • Mechanism of action in the treatment of primary humoral immunodeficiency not fully elucidated.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Mechanism by which IGIV increases platelet counts in the treatment of ITP not fully elucidated.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>130</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>139</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>140</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>142</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> May saturate Fc (crystallizable fragment) receptors on cells of the reticuloendothelial system, resulting in decreased Fc-mediated phagocytosis of antibody-coated cells.<html><head></head><body><sup>130</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>139</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>142</sup></body></html> Altered Fc-receptor affinity for IgG or suppression of antiplatelet antibody production may be involved.<html><head></head><body><sup>139</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>140</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>142</sup></body></html>

  • Mechanism by which IGIV reduces the incidence of acute GVHD following BMT not determined.<html><head></head><body><sup>221</sup></body></html>

  • Mechanism of action of IGIV in the treatment of chronic inflammatory demyelinating polyneuropathy not fully elucidated.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

  • Mechanism of action of IGIV in the treatment of Kawasaki disease is not known,<html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> but possibly may include modulation of cytokine production, neutralization of bacterial superantigens or other etiologic agents, augmentation of T-cell suppressor activity, suppression of antibody synthesis, and provision of anti-idiotypic antibodies.<html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html> IGIV and aspirin appear to have additive anti-inflammatory effects in the treatment of Kawasaki disease.<html><head></head><body><sup>299</sup></body></html>

  • Asceniv 10%: Contains ≥96% IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> Contains glycine and polysorbate 80 as stabilizers.<html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html>

  • Bivigam 10%: Contains ≥96% IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> Contains glycine and polysorbate 80 as stabilizers.<html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html>

  • Carimune NF: Following reconstitution, contains 30–120 mg of protein per mL.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> Contains ≥96% IgG; most of the immunoglobulins are monomeric (7S) IgG; the remainder are dimeric IgG, small amounts of polymeric IgG, traces of IgA and IgM, and immunoglobulin fragments.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses corresponds to that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> Contains sucrose as stabilizing agent.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html>

  • Cutaquig 16.5%: Contains ≥96% IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is approximately 70% IgG1, 25% IgG2, 3% IgG3, and 2% IgG4.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Contains maltose.<html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

  • Cuvitru 20%: Contains 20% protein, of which ≥98% is IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal plasma.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Fc and Fab functions are maintained.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> Contains glycine as stabilizing and buffering agent.<html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html>

  • Flebogamma 5% DIF: Contains ≥97% IgG and trace amounts of IgA (typically <50 mcg/mL) and IgM.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is approximately 66.6% IgG1, 28.5% IgG2, 2.7% IgG3, and 2.2% IgG4.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> Contains sorbitol as stabilizing agent, polyethylene glycol, and trace amounts of sodium.<html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html>

  • Flebogamma 10% DIF: Contains ≥97% IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is approximately 66.6% IgG1, 27.9% IgG2, 3.0% IgG3, and 2.5% IgG4.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> Contains sorbitol as stabilizing agent, polyethylene glycol, and trace amounts of sodium.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html>

  • GamaSTAN: Contains 15–18% protein.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html>

  • Gammagard Liquid 10%: Contains ≥98% IgG, IgA (average 37 mcg/mL), and trace amounts of IgM.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Fc and Fab functions are maintained.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> Contains glycine as stabilizing and buffering agent.<html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html>

  • Gammagard S/D: Following reconstitution, contains approximately 50 mg of protein per mL. Contains ≥90% IgG and trace amounts of IgA (<1 mcg/mL) and IgM.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Fc portion is maintained intact.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> Contains glycine, dextrose, polyethylene glycol, polysorbate 80, and human albumin.<html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html>

  • Gammaked 10%: Contains 9–11% protein stabilized in 0.16–0.24 M glycine;<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> ≥98% of protein content has the electrophoretic mobility of IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal serum;<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> contains trace amounts of fragments, IgA (average 46 mcg/mL), and IgM.<html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html>

  • Gammaplex 5%: Contains ≥95% IgG and <10 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> The IgG subclass distribution is approximately 64% IgG1, 30% IgG2, 5% IgG3, and 1% IgG4.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> Contains sorbitol, glycine, and polysorbate 80 as stabilizers.<html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html>

  • Gammaplex 10%: Contains ≥98% IgG and <20 mcg/mL of IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> The IgG subclass distribution reflects that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> Contains glycine and polysorbate 80 as stabilizers.<html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html>

  • Gamunex-C 10%: Contains 9–11% protein stabilized in 0.16–0.24 M glycine;<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> ≥98% of the protein content has the electrophoretic mobility of IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Contains trace amounts of fragments, IgA (average 46 mcg/mL), and IgM.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> Fc and Fab functions are maintained, but do not activate complement or pre-Kallikrein activity in unspecific manner.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html>

  • Hizentra 20%: Contains 200 mg of protein per mL, of which ≥98% is IgG.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> The Fc and Fab functions of the IgG molecule are retained.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal plasma.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Contains trace amounts of IgA (≤50 mcg/mL).<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> Also contains approximately 250 mmol/L (range 210–290 mmol/L) of l-proline (a nonessential amino acid) as a stabilizer, polysorbate 80 (8–30 mg/L), and trace amounts of sodium.<html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html>

  • Hyqvia (kit containing immune globulin subcutaneous 10% with recombinant human hyaluronidase): Immune globulin subcutaneous component contains ≥98% IgG and trace amounts of IgA (average 37 mcg/mL) and IgM;<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> distribution of IgG subclasses is similar to that of normal serum.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Fab and Fc portions maintained intact and prekallikrein activity not detectable.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> Contains glycine as stabilizing and buffering agent.<html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> Recombinant human hyaluronidase component is a polysaccharide containing 447 amino acids prepared from mammalian cells using recombinant DNA technology.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> Recombinant human hyaluronidase acts locally to temporarily increase permeability of sub-Q tissue to increase dispersion and absorption of the immune globulin subcutaneous component.<html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html>

Advice to Patients

  • Importance of patients understanding potential risks (e.g., thrombosis, hypersensitivity reactions, renal effects, possible transmission of infectious agents) and benefits of immune globulin.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • If the patient and/or caregiver are considered competent to safely administer immune globulin subcutaneous in the home or other appropriate setting, ensure that they receive instructions and training regarding proper dosage and administration.<html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Advise patients of the importance of immediately informing a clinician if symptoms of thrombosis occur, including pain and/or swelling of an arm or leg with warmth over the affected area, discoloration of an arm or leg, unexplained shortness of breath, unexplained rapid pulse, chest pain or discomfort that worsens on deep breathing, numbness or weakness on one side of the body, changes in mental status/confusion, numbness in the face or extremities, weakness or paralysis, severe headache, and/or visual disturbances.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>328</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Instruct patients receiving immune globulin to immediately report symptoms of decreased urine output, sudden weight gain, fluid retention/edema, and/or shortness of breath (which may suggest renal damage) to their clinician.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>249</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Advise patients about the early signs of hypersensitivity (e.g., hives, generalized urticaria, chest tightness, wheezing, hypotension, anaphylaxis) and the importance of immediately contacting clinician if allergic symptoms occur.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Importance of immediately informing clinician if severe headache, neck stiffness, drowsiness, fever, sensitivity to light, painful eye movements, or nausea and vomiting occur since these are possible signs and symptoms of aseptic meningitis syndrome.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

  • Importance of immediately informing clinician if increased heart rate, fatigue, yellowing of skin or eyes, or dark-colored urine occurs since these are possible signs and symptoms of hemolytic anemia.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Advise patients with selective IgA deficiency that IGIV, IGIM, and immune globulin subcutaneous contain trace amounts of IgA and potentially could result in life-threatening allergic reactions if used in patients who have developed antibodies to IgA.<html><head></head><body><sup>154</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>324</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>325</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>326</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Advise patients receiving Cutaquig or Octagam that these preparations contain maltose and may cause falsely-elevated glucose readings when blood glucose monitoring systems based on GDH-PQQ are used; this could result in inappropriate administration of insulin and life-threatening hypoglycemia or could mask true hypoglycemia.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> Importance of using glucose-specific test methods not affected by maltose.<html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>267</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html>

Advise patients that immune globulin may interfere with the immune response to certain live viral vaccines (e.g., MMR, MMRV, varicella virus vaccine live); importance of informing clinician administering vaccines about current or recent immune globulin therapy.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>327</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>331</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Importance of informing clinicians of existing or contemplated concomitant therapy, including prescription and OTC drugs, as well as any concomitant illnesses.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Importance of women informing clinician if they are or plan to become pregnant or plan to breast-feed.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html>

Importance of informing patients of other important precautionary information.<html><head></head><body><sup>125</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>263</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>265</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>266</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>280</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>282</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>292</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>294</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>308</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>332</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>337</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>338</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>339</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>340</sup></body></html> <html><head></head><body><sup>341</sup></body></html> (See Cautions.)

Preparations

Excipients in commercially available drug preparations may have clinically important effects in some individuals; consult specific product labeling for details.

Please refer to the ASHP Drug Shortages Resource Center for information on shortages of one or more of these preparations.
